<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">2017 Pacific hurricane season</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<td class="hlist noprint nowrap" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; padding-top: 3px;"><a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">Pacific hurricane seasons</a><br/>
<a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2015 Pacific hurricane season">2015</a>, <a href="/wiki/2016_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2016 Pacific hurricane season">2016</a>, <b>2017</b>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">2018</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">2019</a></i></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>2017 Pacific hurricane season</b> is an ongoing event in the annual cycle of tropical cyclone formation, in which tropical cyclones form in the northeastern Pacific Ocean. The season officially started on May 15 in the eastern Pacific, and on June 1 in the central Pacific; they will both end on November 30.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-season_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-season-1">[1]</a></sup> These dates conventionally delimit the period of each year when most tropical cyclones form in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">basin</a>. However, the formation of tropical cyclones is possible at any time of the year. This was demonstrated when the first storm, Tropical Storm Adrian, was <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">named</a> on May 10, and became the earliest-known tropical storm in the East Pacific since the advent of satellite imagery. Thus far, the season has seen near-average activity in terms of <a href="/wiki/Accumulated_cyclone_energy" title="Accumulated cyclone energy">ACE</a>, in stark contrast to the extremely active seasons in <a href="/wiki/2014_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2014 Pacific hurricane season">2014</a>, <a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2015 Pacific hurricane season">2015</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2016_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2016 Pacific hurricane season">2016</a>. For the third year in a row, the season featured above average activity in July, with the ACE value being the fifth highest for the month. However, as of November 5, no tropical cyclones have formed in the Central Pacific. If the season ends without a tropical cyclone forming there, it would be the first time since <a href="/wiki/2012_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2012 Pacific hurricane season">2012</a> that this happened. Despite being very active, the season featured the weakest storms since the <a href="/wiki/2013_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2013 Pacific hurricane season">2013 season</a>, with the strongest storm only dropping to 947 millibars.</p>
<p>Beginning this year, the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> has the option to issue advisories, and thus allow watches and warnings to be issued, on disturbances that are not yet tropical cyclones but have a high chance to become one, and are expected to bring tropical storm or hurricane conditions to landmasses within 48 hours. Such systems are classified as "Potential Tropical Cyclones". Advisories on these storms contain the same content, including track forecasts and cyclone watches and warnings, as advisories on active tropical cyclones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> This was first demonstrated on August 29 with the designation of Potential Tropical Cyclone Fourteen-E—which later developed into <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Lidia_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Lidia (2017)">Tropical Storm Lidia</a>—south-southeast of the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p>On May 25, 2017, the <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a> released its annual forecast, predicting a 80% chance of a near- to above-average season in both the Eastern and Central Pacific basins, with a total of 14–20 named storms, 6–11 hurricanes, and 3–7 major hurricanes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[nb 1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-5">[5]</a></sup> During May 28, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Servicio_Meteorol%C3%B3gico_Nacional" title="Servicio Meteorológico Nacional">Servicio Meteorológico Nacional</a> (SMN) issued its first forecast for the season, predicting a total of 16 named storms, 10 hurricanes and 6 major hurricanes to develop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMN_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-SMN-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seasonal_summary">Seasonal summary</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2017_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="Timeline of the 2017 Pacific hurricane season">Timeline of the 2017 Pacific hurricane season</a></div>
<center>
<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map id="timeline_6ab5d95b9d4e607e5cca8e1426114d09" name="timeline_6ab5d95b9d4e607e5cca8e1426114d09">
<area alt="Tropical Storm Lidia (2017)" coords="452,64,516,84" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Lidia_(2017)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Lidia (2017)"/>
<area alt="Saffir–Simpson scale" coords="602,198,761,218" href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" shape="rect" title="Saffir–Simpson scale"/></map><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/6ab5d95b9d4e607e5cca8e1426114d09.png" usemap="#timeline_6ab5d95b9d4e607e5cca8e1426114d09"/></div>
</center>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accumulated_Cyclone_Energy" title="Accumulated Cyclone Energy">Accumulated Cyclone Energy</a> (ACE) for the 2017 Pacific hurricane season, as of Selma's final advisory, is 98.0225 units (97.09 units from the East Pacific and 0.9325 units from the Central Pacific).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[nb 2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although the East Pacific hurricane season does not officially begin until May 15, activity began several days prior with the formation of a tropical depression on May 9. This marked the earliest formation of a tropical cyclone in the basin, surpassing <a href="/wiki/1990_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Alma" title="1990 Pacific hurricane season">1990's Hurricane Alma</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adrianrecord_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Adrianrecord-9">[7]</a></sup> It intensified into Tropical Storm Adrian a few hours later, marking the earliest formation of a named storm on record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[8]</a></sup> Near normal activity occurred in June, with Tropical Storm Calvin formed on June 11, and Hurricane Dora on June 25.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[9]</a></sup> For the third year in a row, July featured above average activity, with the fifth highest ACE value for that month on record. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup> <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">This total was attributed to long lived hurricanes Eugene, Fernanda, Hilary and Irwin. August saw significantly less activity, with only three storms forming in the month; however it featured Hurricane Kenneth, the third major hurricane of the season. September featured four storms, including Hurricane Otis, which became the fourth major hurricane of the season. Activity slowed considerably during the end of the month, only two storms formed after September 23, both of which did not attain hurricane intensity. After Ramon dissipated on October 5, activity ceased with no further storms forming until Tropical Storm Selma, which formed in late October.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Systems">Systems</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Adrian">Tropical Storm Adrian</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Adrian_2017-05-09_1912Z.jpg"><img alt="Adrian 2017-05-09 1912Z.jpg" data-file-height="1302" data-file-width="1002" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Adrian_2017-05-09_1912Z.jpg/150px-Adrian_2017-05-09_1912Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Adrian_2017-05-09_1912Z.jpg/225px-Adrian_2017-05-09_1912Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Adrian_2017-05-09_1912Z.jpg/300px-Adrian_2017-05-09_1912Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Adrian_2017_track.png"><img alt="Adrian 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Adrian_2017_track.png/150px-Adrian_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Adrian_2017_track.png/225px-Adrian_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Adrian_2017_track.png/300px-Adrian_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>May 9 – May 11</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>45 mph (75 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1004 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_off-season_Pacific_hurricanes" title="List of off-season Pacific hurricanes">List of off-season Pacific hurricanes</a></div>
<p>On May 5, the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> (NHC) indicated that an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_pressure_area" title="Low pressure area">area of low pressure</a> was forecast to form south of Mexico over subsequent days, with the possibility of tropical cyclone development thereafter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup> A broad <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_circulation" title="Atmospheric circulation">cyclonic circulation</a> began to develop as expected late on May 7,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup> gradually organizing into the season's first tropical depression by 21:00 UTC on May 9.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup> Upon formation, at which point it was located about 545 mi (875 km) south-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Salina_Cruz" title="Salina Cruz">Salina Cruz, Mexico</a>, the depression became the earliest-forming East Pacific tropical cyclone (east of 140°W) on record. The previous record was held by <a href="/wiki/1990_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Alma" title="1990 Pacific hurricane season">1990's Hurricane Alma</a>, which formed on May 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adrianrecord_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Adrianrecord-9">[7]</a></sup> The depression intensified into Tropical Storm Adrian six hours later, the earliest-known formation of a named storm in eastern Pacific proper since the advent of the satellite era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup> Initially, forecasts expected the small storm to intensify into a powerful hurricane. Shortly after reaching peak intensity early on May 10, an unexpected increase in mid-level <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> caused Adrian to quickly weaken back to a tropical depression by 03:00 UTC on May 11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup> Early on the next day, Adrian degenerated into a remnant low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Beatriz">Tropical Storm Beatriz</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beatriz_2017-06-01_1710Z.jpg"><img alt="Beatriz 2017-06-01 1710Z.jpg" data-file-height="7800" data-file-width="6000" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Beatriz_2017-06-01_1710Z.jpg/150px-Beatriz_2017-06-01_1710Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Beatriz_2017-06-01_1710Z.jpg/225px-Beatriz_2017-06-01_1710Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Beatriz_2017-06-01_1710Z.jpg/300px-Beatriz_2017-06-01_1710Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beatriz_2017_track.png"><img alt="Beatriz 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Beatriz_2017_track.png/150px-Beatriz_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Beatriz_2017_track.png/225px-Beatriz_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Beatriz_2017_track.png/300px-Beatriz_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>May 31 – June 2</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>45 mph (75 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1001 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical wave emerged off the western coast of Africa on May 18 and entered the East Pacific about a week later, where steady organization led to the formation of a tropical depression around 12:00 UTC on May 31. Embedded within southwesterly flow around a large upper-level trough across northern Mexico, the depression moved steadily northeast in a favorable environment, and it intensified into Tropical Storm Beatriz by 06:00 UTC on June 1. After attaining peak winds of 45 mph (75 km/h), the system made landfall around 00:00 UTC on June 2 about 25 miles (40 km) west of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_%C3%81ngel" title="Puerto Ángel">Puerto Ángel</a>. The mountainous terrain of Mexico quickly disrupted Beatriz, and it ultimately dissipated twelve hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Btcr_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Btcr-19">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the state of <a href="/wiki/Oaxaca" title="Oaxaca">Oaxaca</a>, flights out of <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%ADas_de_Huatulco_International_Airport" title="Bahías de Huatulco International Airport">Bahías de Huatulco International Airport</a> were cancelled, and schools were closed until at least June 3. Dozens of roads were rendered impassable due to mudslides and flooding; numerous locales received over 4 in (102 mm) of rain, with a storm total of 19.07 in (484.4 mm) in <a href="/wiki/Huatulco" title="Huatulco">Huatulco</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Btcr_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-Btcr-19">[17]</a></sup> Numerous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landslides" title="Landslides">landslides</a> caused significant disruption across the state, especially by blocking <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Federal_Highway_200" title="Mexican Federal Highway 200">Federal Highway 200</a> at many areas. A landslide in <a href="/wiki/San_Marcial_Ozolotepec" title="San Marcial Ozolotepec">San Marcial Ozolotepec</a> killed two girls and buried several houses, while another in <a href="/wiki/San_Carlos_Yautepec" title="San Carlos Yautepec">San Carlos Yautepec</a> killed a woman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> As of June 4, a total of seven people have been killed—five in Oaxaca and two in <a href="/wiki/Tehuantepec" title="Tehuantepec">Tehuantepec</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup> Less than two weeks after Beatriz, Tropical Storm Calvin affected similar areas of Mexico and inflicted additional damage. Combined damage from the two systems reached at least 70 million pesos (US$3.9 million) in Oaxaca.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Calvin">Tropical Storm Calvin</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Calvin_2017-06-12_2000Z.jpg"><img alt="Calvin 2017-06-12 2000Z.jpg" data-file-height="7200" data-file-width="5600" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Calvin_2017-06-12_2000Z.jpg/150px-Calvin_2017-06-12_2000Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Calvin_2017-06-12_2000Z.jpg/225px-Calvin_2017-06-12_2000Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Calvin_2017-06-12_2000Z.jpg/300px-Calvin_2017-06-12_2000Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Calvin_2017_track.png"><img alt="Calvin 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Calvin_2017_track.png/150px-Calvin_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Calvin_2017_track.png/225px-Calvin_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Calvin_2017_track.png/300px-Calvin_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>June 11 – June 13</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>45 mph (75 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1004 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In the second week of June, the NHC forecast the development of a broad area of low pressure a few hundred miles south of Mexico over the next several days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup> This prediction came to fruition on June 9,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup> and the fledgling disturbance steadily organized into a tropical depression by 12:00 UTC on June 11 while located about 150 mi (240 km) south-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Salina_Cruz" title="Salina Cruz">Salina Cruz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ctcr_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ctcr-25">[23]</a></sup> It was slow to organize initially amid moderate easterly wind shear as it drifted northwestwards;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup> by 18:00 UTC on June 12, however, the tropical depression intensified into Tropical Storm Calvin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ctcr_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ctcr-25">[23]</a></sup> Intensifying slightly to reach winds of 45 mph (75 km/h),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ctcr_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ctcr-25">[23]</a></sup> Calvin made <a href="/wiki/Landfall" title="Landfall">landfall</a> halfway between Salina Cruz and Puerto Ángel, near Paja Blanca, around 00:00 UTC on June 13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup> Just 12 hours later, Calvin dissipated into a remnant low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ctcr_25-3"><a href="#cite_note-Ctcr-25">[23]</a></sup> The remnants of the storm caused heavy rainfall and some flooding in the area,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup> however no fatalities were reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ctcr_25-4"><a href="#cite_note-Ctcr-25">[23]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Dora">Hurricane Dora</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dora_2017-06-26_2020Z.jpg"><img alt="Dora 2017-06-26 2020Z.jpg" data-file-height="10859" data-file-width="8021" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Dora_2017-06-26_2020Z.jpg/150px-Dora_2017-06-26_2020Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Dora_2017-06-26_2020Z.jpg/225px-Dora_2017-06-26_2020Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Dora_2017-06-26_2020Z.jpg/300px-Dora_2017-06-26_2020Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dora_2017_track.png"><img alt="Dora 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Dora_2017_track.png/150px-Dora_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Dora_2017_track.png/225px-Dora_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Dora_2017_track.png/300px-Dora_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>June 25 – June 28</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>90 mph (150 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  981 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On June 21, the NHC began monitoring a broad area of low pressure south of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Tehuantepec" title="Gulf of Tehuantepec">Gulf of Tehuantepec</a> for possible tropical cyclogenesis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup> The disturbance organized into a tropical depression by 03:00 UTC on June 25,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup> and became a tropical storm six hours later, receiving the name <i>Dora</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup> Progressing in a west-northwesterly direction at a steady speed, the storm began a 30-hour period of rapid intensification and became the first hurricane of the season at 09:00 UTC on June 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup> With impressive upper-level outflow and an <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a> apparent on satellite imagery,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> the storm attained peak winds of 90 mph (150 km/h) by late on June 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup> Dora maintained its intensity for a number of hours before beginning to rapidly weaken over cooler sea surface temperatures and in an environment of drier air.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> The storm later degenerated into a remnant low early on June 28, after all of the storm's deep convection had dissipated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>The outer bands of Dora brought heavy rains to <a href="/wiki/Guerrero" title="Guerrero">Guerrero</a>, resulting in flash floods that inundated 20 homes. Overall damage was minor, however.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Eugene">Hurricane Eugene</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
