</tr>
</table>
<p>Hurricane Eugene developed from a disturbance located 765 mi (1,230 km) south of the southern tip of the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a> on July 7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> On the following day, Eugene underwent a period of <a href="/wiki/Rapid_intensification" title="Rapid intensification">rapid intensification</a>; in an 18-hour period starting at 21:00 UTC on July 8, Eugene intensified from a tropical storm with 70 mph (110 km/h) winds to a Category 3 hurricane with 115 mph (185 km/h) winds, making it the first major hurricane of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup> However, by 12 hours later, the entrainment of dry air caused Eugene to weaken to a Category 2 hurricane,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup> and due to traveling over cooler waters, Eugene weakened to a tropical storm on the following day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup> As the coverage of deep convection steadily dwindled, Eugene fell to tropical depression intensity around 15:00 UTC on July 12 and degenerated to a remnant low six hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>Dangerous <a href="/wiki/Rip_current" title="Rip current">rip currents</a> combined with swells of 4 to 8 ft (1.2 to 2.4 m) across southern California resulted in hundreds of rescues. On July 10 alone, lifeguards in <a href="/wiki/Huntington_Beach,_California" title="Huntington Beach, California">Huntington Beach</a> made 200 rescues while 600 were made in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County" title="Los Angeles County">Los Angeles County</a>; lifeguards also responded to 700 medical emergencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Fernanda">Hurricane Fernanda</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fernanda_2017-07-14_2135Z.jpg"><img alt="Fernanda 2017-07-14 2135Z.jpg" data-file-height="7757" data-file-width="5796" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Fernanda_2017-07-14_2135Z.jpg/150px-Fernanda_2017-07-14_2135Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Fernanda_2017-07-14_2135Z.jpg/225px-Fernanda_2017-07-14_2135Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Fernanda_2017-07-14_2135Z.jpg/300px-Fernanda_2017-07-14_2135Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fernanda_2017_track.png"><img alt="Fernanda 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Fernanda_2017_track.png/150px-Fernanda_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Fernanda_2017_track.png/225px-Fernanda_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Fernanda_2017_track.png/300px-Fernanda_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 12 – July 22</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>145 mph (230 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  947 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Late on July 10, the NHC began monitoring a broad area of low pressure several hundred miles southwest of <a href="/wiki/Manzanillo,_Colima" title="Manzanillo, Colima">Manzanillo</a>. Contrary to predictions of gradual development,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup> the disturbance rapidly organized into a tropical depression by 03:00 UTC on July 12,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup> and further strengthened to become Tropical Storm Fernanda around 15:00 UTC that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> The nascent cyclone initially battled moderate northeasterly wind shear, with its low-level circulation displaced to the northeastern edge of the deep convection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup> This period of unfavorable upper-level winds was short-lived, and soon afterwards Fernanda commenced a period of <a href="/wiki/Rapid_intensification" title="Rapid intensification">rapid intensification</a>, intensifying into a hurricane at 21:00 UTC on July 13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> A well-defined eye formed within a growing <a href="/wiki/Central_dense_overcast" title="Central dense overcast">central dense overcast</a>, and Fernanda further intensified into a major hurricane early on July 14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup> Only six hours later, the system was upgraded to a Category 4 hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup> At 10.9°N, Fernanda became the second strongest hurricane to occur at such a low latitude in the Eastern Pacific, only behind <a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Olaf" title="2015 Pacific hurricane season">2015's Hurricane Olaf</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>With expansive upper-level outflow and spiral bands, a distinct eye, and a symmetric central dense overcast, Fernanda attained peak winds of 145 mph (230 km/h) around 03:00 UTC on July 15.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> A series of microwave passes around that time began to indicate the formation of a secondary eyewall that halted the cyclone's development as it tracked west-northwest to northwest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> The eyewall replacement cycle concluded early on July 16, allowing Fernanda to remain a powerful hurricane amid favorable environmental conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup> By late on July 18, however, cooler ocean temperatures and a more stable environment prompted the storm's weakening trend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup> Fernanda fell below hurricane intensity shortly before entering the Central Pacific as it succumbed to stronger southwesterly wind shear,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup> and after failing to produce sustained deep convection, degenerated to a remnant low about 500 miles (805 km) east of <a href="/wiki/Hilo,_Hawaii" title="Hilo, Hawaii">Hilo, Hawaii</a>, by 21:00 UTC on July 22.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Greg">Tropical Storm Greg</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greg_2017-07-21_1835Z.jpg"><img alt="Greg 2017-07-21 1835Z.jpg" data-file-height="5665" data-file-width="4417" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Greg_2017-07-21_1835Z.jpg/150px-Greg_2017-07-21_1835Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Greg_2017-07-21_1835Z.jpg/225px-Greg_2017-07-21_1835Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Greg_2017-07-21_1835Z.jpg/300px-Greg_2017-07-21_1835Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greg_Pacific_2017_track.png"><img alt="Greg Pacific 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Greg_Pacific_2017_track.png/150px-Greg_Pacific_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Greg_Pacific_2017_track.png/225px-Greg_Pacific_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Greg_Pacific_2017_track.png/300px-Greg_Pacific_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 17 – July 26</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>60 mph (95 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1001 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On July 12, the NHC forecast the formation of a broad area of low pressure south of Mexico over subsequent days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> The disturbance formed two days later and slowly organized into a tropical depression by 15:00 UTC on July 17.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> The cyclone battled strong west-northwesterly wind shear after formation, intensifying into Tropical Storm Greg by 09:00 UTC on July 18 as deep convection burst near the center, but remained steady state for several days thereafter despite continued predictions of intensification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> Ultimately, given global models' poor handling of the environment, NHC lowered their intensity forecast for Greg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> The cyclone continued west for the remainder of its life and maintained a similar convective structure, with intermittent bursts of deep convection near the center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> Approaching the Central Pacific, Greg's low-level circulation became increasingly difficult to locate as it moved into a cooler, drier environment intertwined by increasing southerly wind shear, and the system weakened to a tropical depression around 21:00 UTC on July 25.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> It degenerated to a remnant low 24 hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Eight-E">Tropical Depression Eight-E</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:08E_2017-07-18_1805Z.jpg"><img alt="08E 2017-07-18 1805Z.jpg" data-file-height="1376" data-file-width="1084" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/08E_2017-07-18_1805Z.jpg/150px-08E_2017-07-18_1805Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/08E_2017-07-18_1805Z.jpg/225px-08E_2017-07-18_1805Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/08E_2017-07-18_1805Z.jpg/300px-08E_2017-07-18_1805Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:08E_2017_track.png"><img alt="08E 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/08E_2017_track.png/150px-08E_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/08E_2017_track.png/225px-08E_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/08E_2017_track.png/300px-08E_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 18 – July 20</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>35 mph (55 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1007 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A low-pressure trough began producing disorganized convection over the waters of the Pacific Ocean, well to the south of <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a>, on July 14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> Despite only marginally conducive environmental conditions, the disturbance began to show signs of organization two days later,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup> and it attained tropical depression status by 15:00 UTC on July 18.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> Strong west-northwesterly <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> confined the storm's intermittent bursts of convection well to the southwest of its low-level circulation, and the depression consequently failed to produce winds above 35 mph (55 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup> The system's center later degenerated into a low-pressure trough within the <a href="/wiki/Intertropical_Convergence_Zone" title="Intertropical Convergence Zone">Intertropical Convergence Zone</a>, prompting the NHC to discontinue advisories at 21:00 UTC on July 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Hilary">Hurricane Hilary</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hilary_2017-07-25_2015Z.jpg"><img alt="Hilary 2017-07-25 2015Z.jpg" data-file-height="6393" data-file-width="5140" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Hilary_2017-07-25_2015Z.jpg/150px-Hilary_2017-07-25_2015Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Hilary_2017-07-25_2015Z.jpg/225px-Hilary_2017-07-25_2015Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Hilary_2017-07-25_2015Z.jpg/300px-Hilary_2017-07-25_2015Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hilary_2017_track.png"><img alt="Hilary 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Hilary_2017_track.png/150px-Hilary_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Hilary_2017_track.png/225px-Hilary_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Hilary_2017_track.png/300px-Hilary_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 21 – July 31</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>105 mph (165 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  972 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Part of an exceptionally active July, the NHC began highlighting the far eastern reaches of the Pacific basin on July 19 for tropical development in later days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Daniel_P._Brown_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Daniel_P._Brown-74">[72]</a></sup> A large area of disturbed weather progressed westward across <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a> later that day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup> steadily organizing into a tropical depression by 15:00 UTC on July 21.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup> The cyclone failed to organize immediately after formation, and its low-level center migrated to the southern extent of associated convection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup> By 03:00 UTC on July 23, though, better defined banding features and a more organized convective structure led the NHC to designate the system as Tropical Storm Hilary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup> Over the coming hours, the cyclone's convective structure evolved into a small central dense overcast while hints of an eye became apparent;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> in accordance with satellite estimates, Hilary was upgraded to a hurricane at 09:00 UTC on July 24.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> A moist environment and warm ocean waters propelled Hilary to its peak as a Category 2 hurricane with winds of 105 mph (165 km/h) 24 hours later, at which time its core was most symmetric.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> After maintaining its intensity, the hurricane began to weaken late on July 26 as northerly wind shear increased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> It fell back to tropical storm intensity around 03:00 UTC on July 27 and ultimately degenerated to a remnant low four days later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Irwin">Hurricane Irwin</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Irwin_2017-07-25_2120Z.jpg"><img alt="Irwin 2017-07-25 2120Z.jpg" data-file-height="10039" data-file-width="8093" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Irwin_2017-07-25_2120Z.jpg/150px-Irwin_2017-07-25_2120Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Irwin_2017-07-25_2120Z.jpg/225px-Irwin_2017-07-25_2120Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Irwin_2017-07-25_2120Z.jpg/300px-Irwin_2017-07-25_2120Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Irwin_2017_track.png"><img alt="Irwin 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1907" data-file-width="3000" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Irwin_2017_track.png/150px-Irwin_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Irwin_2017_track.png/225px-Irwin_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Irwin_2017_track.png/300px-Irwin_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 22 – August 1</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>90 mph (150 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  980 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On July 16, the NHC highlighted the expected formation of an area of low pressure south of Mexico later that week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup> A tropical wave began producing disorganized cloudiness three days later,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Daniel_P._Brown_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-Daniel_P._Brown-74">[72]</a></sup> and the broad system slowly organized into a tropical depression by 15:00 UTC on July 22.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup> Its structure changed little after formation, impinged by strong wind shear; despite this, satellite wind data indicated the cyclone intensified into Tropical Storm Irwin by 09:00 UTC on July 23.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup> Over the next 24 hours, deep convection began to wrap around the center and a mid-level eye formed as environmental conditions improved;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> by 09:00 UTC on July 25, Irwin intensified into a hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup> Although coolest cloudtops were located in the western semicircle of the system, a well-defined eye and convection in the eyewall propelled Irwin to its peak with winds of 90 mph (150 km/h) late on July 25.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup> Almost immediately, outflow from nearby Hurricane Hilary increased wind shear over the system and caused it to begin weakening;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup> Irwin rapidly fell to tropical storm strength around 15:00 UTC on July 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup> Contrary to projections of continued weakening, however, the storm's cloud pattern maintained or even improved over subsequent days as it passed over marginal ocean temperatures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup> Finally, after losing its deep convection and being reduced to a swirl of low-level clouds, Irwin was declared a remnant low around 21:00 UTC on August 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Eleven-E">Tropical Depression Eleven-E</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:11E_2017-08-04_2015Z.jpg"><img alt="11E 2017-08-04 2015Z.jpg" data-file-height="6193" data-file-width="4577" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/11E_2017-08-04_2015Z.jpg/150px-11E_2017-08-04_2015Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/11E_2017-08-04_2015Z.jpg/225px-11E_2017-08-04_2015Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/11E_2017-08-04_2015Z.jpg/300px-11E_2017-08-04_2015Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:11E_2017_track.png"><img alt="11E 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/11E_2017_track.png/150px-11E_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/11E_2017_track.png/225px-11E_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/11E_2017_track.png/300px-11E_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 4 – August 5</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>35 mph (55 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1004 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On July 28, the NHC advertised the likely development of an area of low pressure well south of Mexico over subsequent days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> An area of disorganized showers and thunderstorms associated with a tropical wave materialized three days later, but little change occurred thereafter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup> Early on August 3, a surface circulation formed in association with concentrating convection,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup> and this process led to the formation of a tropical depression by 15:00 UTC the next day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[96]</a></sup> The newly formed cyclone did not intensify after designation, and its low- and mid-level circulations separated by over 265 mi (425 km) on August 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup> Falling short of the tropical cyclone criteria, the short-lived depression was declared a remnant low at 21:00 UTC that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Jova">Tropical Storm Jova</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jova_2017-08-11_Suomi_NPP.jpg"><img alt="Jova 2017-08-11 Suomi NPP.jpg" data-file-height="2862" data-file-width="2161" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Jova_2017-08-11_Suomi_NPP.jpg/150px-Jova_2017-08-11_Suomi_NPP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Jova_2017-08-11_Suomi_NPP.jpg/225px-Jova_2017-08-11_Suomi_NPP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Jova_2017-08-11_Suomi_NPP.jpg/300px-Jova_2017-08-11_Suomi_NPP.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jova_2017_track.png"><img alt="Jova 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Jova_2017_track.png/150px-Jova_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Jova_2017_track.png/225px-Jova_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Jova_2017_track.png/300px-Jova_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 12 – August 14</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>40 mph (65 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1003 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The NHC began monitoring a strong tropical wave over the eastern Caribbean on August 3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup> The feature pushed westward, developing into <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Franklin" title="Hurricane Franklin">Hurricane Franklin</a> before making landfall on the <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n" title="Yucatán">Yucatán</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup> and attaining its peak as a Category 1 hurricane before making landfall near <a href="/wiki/Vega_de_Alatorre" title="Vega de Alatorre">Vega de Alatorre, Veracruz</a> on August 10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup> Although its low-level circulation dissipated, the NHC in days prior noted the potential for Franklin's mid-level remnants to reform in the East Pacific.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup> The remnants of Franklin induced a surface low off the coast of southwestern Mexico on August 11, and steady organization led to the formation of Tropical Storm Jova by 03:00 UTC the next day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup> On a westward course, Jova was plagued by strong wind shear from an area of high pressure over northwestern Mexico, with a very disorganized appearance on satellite.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup> After lacking sufficient organization to be declared a tropical cyclone, the storm was declared a remnant low around 03:00 UTC on August 14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Kenneth">Hurricane Kenneth</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kenneth_2017-08-20_2156Z.jpg"><img alt="Kenneth 2017-08-20 2156Z.jpg" data-file-height="8771" data-file-width="6077" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Kenneth_2017-08-20_2156Z.jpg/150px-Kenneth_2017-08-20_2156Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Kenneth_2017-08-20_2156Z.jpg/225px-Kenneth_2017-08-20_2156Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Kenneth_2017-08-20_2156Z.jpg/300px-Kenneth_2017-08-20_2156Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kenneth_2017_track.png"><img alt="Kenneth 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Kenneth_2017_track.png/150px-Kenneth_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Kenneth_2017_track.png/225px-Kenneth_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Kenneth_2017_track.png/300px-Kenneth_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 18 – August 23</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>130 mph (215 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  952 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On August 12, the NHC noted the potential for an area of low pressure to form well south of <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a> during the following days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup> A large area of disturbed weather developed two days later as predicted;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup> however, organization was slow to occur, and a tropical depression only formed four days later, around 15:00 UTC on August 18.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup> The newly formed cyclone embarked on a west to west-northwest course, intensifying into Tropical Storm Kenneth early on August 19 and further into a hurricane by 15:00 UTC on August 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup> Despite forecasts of only slight additional intensification,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup> Kenneth rapidly intensified, with the <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye feature</a> warming dramatically and the surrounding cloud tops cooling. The cyclone attained <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson scale">major hurricane</a> strength around 03:00 UTC on August 21,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup> and six hours later reached its peak as a Category 4 hurricane with sustained winds of 130 mph (215 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup> Progressively cooler <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">sea surface temperatures</a> and increasing <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> caused Kenneth to steadily weaken following the intensification trend, with its inner core eroding and low-level circulation becoming displaced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup> By 21:00 UTC on August 22, the storm weakened below hurricane strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> The following day, at 21:00 UTC, Kenneth was declared post-tropical.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Lidia">Tropical Storm Lidia</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lidia_2017-08-31_2023Z.jpg"><img alt="Lidia 2017-08-31 2023Z.jpg" data-file-height="9706" data-file-width="6734" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Lidia_2017-08-31_2023Z.jpg/150px-Lidia_2017-08-31_2023Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Lidia_2017-08-31_2023Z.jpg/225px-Lidia_2017-08-31_2023Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Lidia_2017-08-31_2023Z.jpg/300px-Lidia_2017-08-31_2023Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lidia_2017_track.png"><img alt="Lidia 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Lidia_2017_track.png/150px-Lidia_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Lidia_2017_track.png/225px-Lidia_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Lidia_2017_track.png/300px-Lidia_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 31 – September 3</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>65 mph (100 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  987 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Lidia_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Lidia (2017)">Tropical Storm Lidia (2017)</a></div>
<p>On August 29, the NHC monitored a potential area of Tropical Cyclone development near the coast of <a href="/wiki/Baja_California" title="Baja California">Baja California</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Watch" title="Tropical Storm Watch">Tropical Storm Watches</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Watch" title="Hurricane Watch">Hurricane Watches</a> stretching from <a href="/wiki/Todos_Santos,_Baja_California_Sur" title="Todos Santos, Baja California Sur">Todos Santos</a> to <a href="/wiki/Los_Barriles,_Baja_California_Sur" title="Los Barriles, Baja California Sur">Los Barriles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">The NHC initiated advisories on Tropical Storm Lidia at 00:00 <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a> on August 31 about 180 mi (290 km) south-southeast of the southern tip of the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a>. Favorable conditions allowed Lidia to intensify, and by 21:00 UTC on August 31, the storm peaked with <a href="/wiki/Maximum_sustained_wind" title="Maximum sustained wind">maximum sustained winds</a> of 65 mph (100 km/h) and a minimum <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure" title="Atmospheric pressure">atmospheric pressure</a> of 987 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (29.1 <a href="/wiki/Inch_of_mercury" title="Inch of mercury">inHg</a>). Around 12:00 UTC on the following day, Lidia made <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a> near <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Chale" title="Puerto Chale">Puerto Chale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Sur" title="Baja California Sur">Baja California Sur</a>, at the same intensity. The cyclone weakened significantly while traversing the mountainous terrain of the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a>, and by early on September 2, deep convection was mainly limited to a few strong clusters near the center. Around that time, Lidia briefly moved offshore, before making another landfall near <a href="/wiki/Punta_Abreojos" title="Punta Abreojos">Punta Abreojos</a> a few hours later. By that time, Lidia had weakened steadily, and emerged over the Pacific Ocean on September 2. However, Lidia continued to weaken due to cold <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperatures" title="Sea surface temperatures">sea surface temperatures</a>. After failing to produce deep convection for about 12–15 hours, the NHC declared that Lidia had degenerated into a remnant low-pressure area at 09:00 UTC on September 2 about 40 mi (65 km/h) southwest of Punta Baja, Baja California.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Otis">Hurricane Otis</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Otis_2017-09-17_1915Z.jpg"><img alt="Otis 2017-09-17 1915Z.jpg" data-file-height="7987" data-file-width="5754" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Otis_2017-09-17_1915Z.jpg/150px-Otis_2017-09-17_1915Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Otis_2017-09-17_1915Z.jpg/225px-Otis_2017-09-17_1915Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Otis_2017-09-17_1915Z.jpg/300px-Otis_2017-09-17_1915Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Otis_2017_track.png"><img alt="Otis 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Otis_2017_track.png/150px-Otis_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Otis_2017_track.png/225px-Otis_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Otis_2017_track.png/300px-Otis_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 11 – September 19</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>115 mph (185 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  965 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On September 8, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katia_(2017)" title="Hurricane Katia (2017)">Hurricane Katia</a> of the Atlantic made landfall on Mexico, dissipating on September 9. However, its mid-level circulation survived, and eventually spawned an area of low pressure off the coast of Mexico. On September 11, the system organized into Tropical Depression Fifteen-E. During the next several days, the depression slowly drifted westward, before strengthening into Tropical Storm Otis on September 16. While only marginal strengthening was forecast, Otis unexpectedly rapidly intensified into a Category 2 hurricane by 17:00 UTC on September 17, despite lower ocean temperatures, drier air, and increased wind shear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup> Otis continued to intensify into a Category 3 major hurricane by 03:00 UTC on September 18, developing a well-defined eye with a diameter of 10 nautical miles (12 mi; 19 km).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup> By 21:00 UTC on September 18, Otis had rapidly degenerated back into a tropical storm with maximum sustained winds of 40 knots (46 mph; 74 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> Twelve hours after developing a well-defined eye, Otis started weakening at a remarkable rate, losing most of its deep convection from low ocean surface temperatures until it became a remnant low on September 19, due to a lack of convection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Max">Hurricane Max</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Max_2017-09-14_1705Z.jpg"><img alt="Max 2017-09-14 1705Z.jpg" data-file-height="10753" data-file-width="7475" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Max_2017-09-14_1705Z.jpg/150px-Max_2017-09-14_1705Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Max_2017-09-14_1705Z.jpg/225px-Max_2017-09-14_1705Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Max_2017-09-14_1705Z.jpg/300px-Max_2017-09-14_1705Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Max_2017_track.png"><img alt="Max 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Max_2017_track.png/150px-Max_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Max_2017_track.png/225px-Max_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Max_2017_track.png/300px-Max_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 13 – September 15</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>85 mph (140 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  985 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On September 9, the NHC mentioned the possibility for an area of low pressure to form south of Mexico over later days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup> A trough of low pressure materialized the next day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> steadily organizing into a tropical depression near the southwestern coast of Mexico around 15:00 UTC on September 13. Despite forecasts of little or no intensification,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> the newly formed cyclone intensified into Tropical Storm Max six hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup> Quick intensification ensued as the storm improved in structure and developed a well-defined eye, prompting the NHC to upgrade Max to a hurricane around 12:00 UTC on September 14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup> After attaining peak winds of 85 mph (140 km/h),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup> the hurricane moved ashore the coastline of Guerrero at a slightly reduced strength around 21:00 UTC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup> The mountainous terrain of inland Mexico severely disrupted Max's circulation, causing it to degenerate by 09:00 UTC on September 15.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>In preparation for Max, about 788 people evacuated to temporary shelters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ElManana_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-ElManana-131">[129]</a></sup> Throughout Guerrero, over 1,500 homes were inundated by floodwaters or damaged by strong winds that ripped off roofs. Over 100 trees were downed, mudslides and sinkholes closed several roads (including <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Federal_Highway_200" title="Mexican Federal Highway 200">Mexican Federal Highway 200</a>), and telephone service was cut. At the height of the storm, 126,503 <a href="/wiki/Comisi%C3%B3n_Federal_de_Electricidad" title="Comisión Federal de Electricidad">Comisión Federal de Electricidad</a> customers lost electricity. A bridge between <a href="/wiki/Cruz_Grande" title="Cruz Grande">Cruz Grande</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copala,_Guerrero" title="Copala, Guerrero">Copala</a> was severely damaged, and access to <a href="/wiki/Juchit%C3%A1n_de_Zaragoza" title="Juchitán de Zaragoza">Juchitán de Zaragoza</a> was severed due to a flooded highway. One of 17 rapidly-rising rivers swept away a residence and two neighbors who attempted to rescue the homeowner; one of the neighbors died, constituting one of two deaths attributed to the storm. At least 3,000 residents across five municipalities in Guerrero were stranded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ElManana_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-ElManana-131">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup> Waves of 10–16 ft (3–5 m) battered the coastline, where six ships were sunk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Norma">Hurricane Norma</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Norma_2017-09-15_2055Z.jpg"><img alt="Norma 2017-09-15 2055Z.jpg" data-file-height="7823" data-file-width="5583" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Norma_2017-09-15_2055Z.jpg/150px-Norma_2017-09-15_2055Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Norma_2017-09-15_2055Z.jpg/225px-Norma_2017-09-15_2055Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Norma_2017-09-15_2055Z.jpg/300px-Norma_2017-09-15_2055Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Norma_2017_track.png"><img alt="Norma 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Norma_2017_track.png/150px-Norma_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Norma_2017_track.png/225px-Norma_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Norma_2017_track.png/300px-Norma_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 14 – September 20</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>75 mph (120 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  985 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On September 10, the NHC started to monitor an area of low pressure well south of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manzanillo,_Mexico" title="Manzanillo, Mexico">Manzanillo, Mexico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup> The disturbance gradually organized during the following days and by 09:00 UTC on September 14 the system was noted to develop a well-defined center and spiral banding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> This led to the formation of Tropical Storm Norma, skipping tropical depression status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup> The newly formed tropical storm continued to intensify at a steady pace while it moved slowly northward, becoming a category 1 hurricane by 03:00 UTC on September 16 and reaching winds of 75 mph (120 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup> At this time warnings were being required for the southern portions of the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a> as Norma was forecast to become a major hurricane and make landfall in the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup> However, its broad circulation and the entrainment of dry air quickly became an impediment in doing so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> Norma then weakened back to a tropical storm at 21:00 UTC later that day while becoming stationary, though a developing ridge over <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> began to move the storm slowly towards the north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup> Norma maintained its intensity the next day and continued being slowly steered by the ridge towards a northwesterly to west-northwesterly path, all tropical storm warnings were discontinued as Norma started to shift its track more to the west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup> The cyclone continued weakening for several days as it slowly drifted to the west, until finally being declared a remnant low at 03:00 UTC on September 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Pilar">Tropical Storm Pilar</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pilar_2017-09-24_1740Z.jpg"><img alt="Pilar 2017-09-24 1740Z.jpg" data-file-height="5600" data-file-width="4400" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Pilar_2017-09-24_1740Z.jpg/150px-Pilar_2017-09-24_1740Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Pilar_2017-09-24_1740Z.jpg/225px-Pilar_2017-09-24_1740Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Pilar_2017-09-24_1740Z.jpg/300px-Pilar_2017-09-24_1740Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pilar_2017_track.png"><img alt="Pilar 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Pilar_2017_track.png/150px-Pilar_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Pilar_2017_track.png/225px-Pilar_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Pilar_2017_track.png/300px-Pilar_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 23 – September 25</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>45 mph (75 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1002 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>During the week of September 18, the NHC began monitoring a tropical wave,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup> as it spawned a broad area of low pressure located offshore of the southwestern coast of <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup> The disturbance lacked any significant organization until September 23 at around 21:00 UTC when the system was noted to developed surface winds of over 35 mph (55 km/h) becoming Tropical Depression Eighteen-E.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> The depression organized into a tropical storm six hours later and was given the name <i>Pilar</i>, the sixteenth named storm of the annual Pacific hurricane season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup> Thereafter, despite having a disorganized appearance on satellite, Pilar's winds increased in strength, and it reached its peak with sustained winds of 45 mph (75 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup> By 09:00 UTC on September 24, Pilar continued to track north along the coast, with warnings being issued for the southwestern coast of Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup> However, early on September 25, these warnings were discontinued,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup> as Tropical Storm Pilar showed signs of weakening mainly due to land interaction, and was reduced to a tropical depression before ultimately dissipating at around 21:00 UTC later that same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup> Although Pilar did not make landfall as a tropical cyclone, heavy rainfall was reported in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Vallarta,_Mexico" title="Puerto Vallarta, Mexico">Puerto Vallarta, Mexico</a>, northeast of <a href="/wiki/Islas_Mar%C3%ADas" title="Islas Marías">Islas Marías</a> and in other areas along the Mexican coastline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Ramon">Tropical Storm Ramon</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ramon_2017-10-04_1945Z.jpg"><img alt="Ramon 2017-10-04 1945Z.jpg" data-file-height="8865" data-file-width="6721" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ramon_2017-10-04_1945Z.jpg/150px-Ramon_2017-10-04_1945Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ramon_2017-10-04_1945Z.jpg/225px-Ramon_2017-10-04_1945Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ramon_2017-10-04_1945Z.jpg/300px-Ramon_2017-10-04_1945Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ramon_2017_track.png"><img alt="Ramon 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Ramon_2017_track.png/150px-Ramon_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Ramon_2017_track.png/225px-Ramon_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Ramon_2017_track.png/300px-Ramon_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 4 – October 5</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>45 mph (75 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1002 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On October 3, the NHC noted a high chance of tropical development in an area of low pressure, to the south of Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup> The system increased in intensity and became Tropical Storm Ramon early on October 4, skipping tropical depression status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup> Due to wind shear from a large anticyclone to its north, the storm did not intensify much further.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup> Although it was forecast to linger over open waters as it moved westward, this did not occur and the system quickly grew disorganized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup> Ramon weakened into a tropical depression later on the same day, having lasted as a tropical storm only for 18 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup> As it moved westward, Ramon continued to weaken, until it finally degenerated into a trough of low pressure on October 5, and the National Hurricane Center issued its last advisory on the degenerated system at 09:00 UTC, on the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Storm_names">Storm names</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">Tropical cyclone naming</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_tropical_cyclone_naming" title="History of tropical cyclone naming">History of tropical cyclone naming</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names" title="List of historic tropical cyclone names">List of historic tropical cyclone names</a></div>
<p>The following names will be used for named storms that form in the northeastern Pacific Ocean during 2017. <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Pacific_hurricane_names" title="List of retired Pacific hurricane names">Retired names</a>, if any, will be announced by the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> in the spring of 2018. The names not retired from this list will be used again in the 2023 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup> This same list was used in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2011 Pacific hurricane season">2011 season</a>.</p>

<p>For storms that form in the <a href="/wiki/Central_Pacific_Hurricane_Center" title="Central Pacific Hurricane Center">Central Pacific Hurricane Center</a>'s area of responsibility, encompassing the area between <a href="/wiki/140th_meridian_west" title="140th meridian west">140 degrees west</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a>, all names are used in a series of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_tropical_cyclone_names#Central_Pacific" title="List of tropical cyclone names">four rotating lists</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup> The next four names slated for use are shown below.</p>

<li><span style="color:#666666">Hone <i>(unused)</i></span></li>
</ul>

<p>The usage of the Atlantic storm name "Don", and the name "Hilary", in July garnered some negative attention relating to <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">United States President</a> <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, and former Presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a>. People also took to Twitter to poke fun at the names and both individuals, with political jokes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_effects">Season effects</span></h2>
<p>This is a table of all the storms that have formed in the 2017 Pacific hurricane season. It includes their duration, names, landfall(s), denoted in parentheses, damages, and death totals. Deaths in parentheses are additional and indirect (an example of an indirect death would be a traffic accident), but were still related to that storm. Damage and deaths include totals while the storm was extratropical, a wave, or a low, and all the damage figures are in 2017 USD.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A major hurricane is a storm that ranks as Category 3 or higher on the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson scale">Saffir–Simpson scale</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The totals represent the sum of the squares for every (sub)tropical storm's intensity of over 33 knots (38 mph, 61 km/h), divided by 10,000. Calculations are provided at <a href="/wiki/Talk:2017_Pacific_hurricane_season/ACE_calcs" title="Talk:2017 Pacific hurricane season/ACE calcs">Talk:2017 Pacific hurricane season/ACE calcs</a>.</span></li>
</ol>
